That‚Äôs not correct.

He had weekend overnight unsupervised visits pursuant to a court order from Santa Cruz, which was issued after a FCS investigation from which the Court issued orders, and which is attached; the matter was continued for further hearings about custody to June, 2019. The Court did not issue permanent custody orders. Then the matter in Santa Cruz was pre-empted by the SF investigation and dependency based on Mother‚Äôs false allegations of child sexual abuse. Father passed a polygraph exam indicating he did not sexually abuse his daughter, is not listed on the CACI, and has done everything the HSA has asked of him since the case started.

To now assert that Father is not entitled to reunification is disingenuous, legally unsupported, and not in the best interests of the child. Once the dependency court takes jurisdiction, as it has done here, all prior orders regarding custody and visitation are no longer applicable. Father is entitled to be assessed for placement, custody, and whatever else the Court may order that is in the best interests of the child.

Thank you,

Nick
